It represents the page as a tree of objects that JavaScript can manipulate. When a web page loads, the browser creates a DOM of the page, which allows JavaScript to access and change the HTML elements, attributes, and CSS styles dynamically.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Key Concept:</strong> Think of the DOM as a bridge between your HTML and JavaScript. HTML provides the structure, and through the DOM, JavaScript can read, modify, add, or delete elements and content.\n                </div>\n\n                <h3>DOM Tree Structure</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Consider this HTML:\n&lt;html&gt;\n  &lt;head&gt;\n    &lt;title&gt;My Page&lt;/title&gt;\n  &lt;/head&gt;\n  &lt;body&gt;\n    &lt;div id="container"&gt;\n      &lt;h1&gt;Hello&lt;/h1&gt;\n      &lt;p class="text"&gt;World&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n  &lt;/body&gt;\n&lt;/html&gt;\n\n// The DOM represents this as a tree:\n// document\n//   └── html\n//        ├── head\n//        │    └── title\n//        │         └── "My Page" (text node)\n//        └── body\n//             └── div (id="container")\n//                  ├── h1\n//                  │    └── "Hello"\n//                  └── p (class="text")\n//                       └── "World"</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Selecting Elements</h2>\n                <p>Before manipulating elements, you need to select them:</p>\n                \n                <h3>Modern Methods (Preferred)</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// querySelector - first matching element\nconst header = document.querySelector("h1");\nconst container = document.querySelector("#container");\nconst text = document.querySelector(".text");\nconst firstParagraph = document.querySelector("p.intro");\n\n// querySelectorAll - all matching elements (NodeList)\nconst allParagraphs = document.querySelectorAll("p");\nconst allItems = document.querySelectorAll(".list-item");\n\n// Iterate over NodeList\nallParagraphs.forEach(paragraph => {\n    console.log(paragraph.textContent);\n});\n\n// Convert NodeList to Array for more methods\nconst paragraphsArray = Array.from(allParagraphs);\nconst filtered = paragraphsArray.filter(p => p.textContent.length > 50);</code></pre>\n                </div>\n\n                <h3>Traditional Methods</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// getElementById - fastest for IDs\nconst element = document.getElementById("myId");\n\n// getElementsByClassName - returns HTMLCollection (live)\nconst items = document.getElementsByClassName("item");\n\n// getElementsByTagName - returns HTMLCollection (live)\nconst divs = document.getElementsByTagName("div");\n\n// Convert HTMLCollection to Array\nconst itemsArray = Array.from(items);\n\n// Live collection updates automatically\nconst liveList = document.getElementsByClassName("item");\nconsole.log(liveList.length);  // 3\n// Add new element with class "item"\nconsole.log(liveList.length);  // 4 (automatically updated)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>querySelector vs getElementById:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>querySelector</code> - More flexible, uses CSS selectors, returns first match</li>\n                        <li><code>getElementById</code> - Faster, only for IDs, single element</li>\n                        <li><code>querySelectorAll</code> - Returns static NodeList</li>\n                        <li><code>getElementsBy*</code> - Returns live HTMLCollection</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Traversing the DOM</h2>\n                <p>Navigate between related elements:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const element = document.querySelector(".container");\n\n// Parent element\nconst parent = element.parentElement;\nconst closestParent = element.closest(".wrapper");  // Find ancestor\n\n// Children\nconst children = element.children;        // HTMLCollection of child elements\nconst firstChild = element.firstElementChild;\nconst lastChild = element.lastElementChild;\n\n// Siblings\nconst nextSibling = element.nextElementSibling;\nconst previousSibling = element.previousElementSibling;\n\n// Check if element has children\nconst hasChildren = element.hasChildNodes();\n\n// Example: Get all siblings\nfunction getAllSiblings(element) {\n    const siblings = [];\n    let sibling = element.parentElement.firstElementChild;\n    \n    while (sibling) {\n        if (sibling !== element) {\n            siblings.push(sibling);\n        }\n        sibling = sibling.nextElementSibling;\n    }\n    \n    return siblings;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Modifying Element Content</h2>\n                <p>Change what\'s inside elements:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const element = document.querySelector("#content");\n\n// textContent - gets/sets text only\nconsole.log(element.textContent);   // Get text\nelement.textContent = "New text";   // Set text (safe from XSS)\n\n// innerHTML - gets/sets HTML\nconsole.log(element.innerHTML);     // Get HTML including tags\nelement.innerHTML = "&lt;strong&gt;Bold text&lt;/strong&gt;";  // Parses HTML\n\n// outerHTML - includes the element itself\nconsole.log(element.outerHTML);     // Includes the element tag\nelement.outerHTML = "&lt;div&gt;Replaced&lt;/div&gt;";  // Replaces element\n\n// innerText - similar to textContent but respects CSS styling\nconsole.log(element.innerText);     // Respects visibility: hidden\n\n// Differences in action\nconst div = document.querySelector("#example");\ndiv.innerHTML = "&lt;span style=\'display:none\'&gt;Hidden&lt;/span&gt;";\n\nconsole.log(div.textContent);  // "Hidden" (includes hidden text)\nconsole.log(div.innerText);    // "" (respects display:none)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Security Warning:</strong> Never use <code>innerHTML</code> with user input! It can lead to XSS (Cross-Site Scripting) attacks.  // camelCase, not kebab-case\nelement.style.fontSize = "20px";\nelement.style.padding = "10px 20px";\n\n// Remove inline style\nelement.style.color = "";  // Empty string removes it\n\n// Multiple styles\nObject.assign(element.style, {\n    color: "white",\n    backgroundColor: "navy",\n    padding: "20px",\n    borderRadius: "5px"\n});\n\n// Get computed style (actual applied styles)\nconst computed = window.getComputedStyle(element);\nconsole.log(computed.color);           // Actual color\nconsole.log(computed.backgroundColor); // Actual background\n\n// CSS custom properties (variables)\nelement.style.setProperty("--main-color", "purple");\nconst mainColor = element.style.getPropertyValue("--main-color");\n\n// cssText - set all styles at once\nelement.style.cssText = "color: white; background: navy; padding: 10px;";\n\n// Toggle visibility\nelement.style.display = "none";        // Hide\nelement.style.display = "block";       // Show\nelement.style.visibility = "hidden";   // Hide (keeps space)\nelement.style.visibility = "visible";  // Show\n\n// Better approach: Use classes for styles\n// CSS: .hidden { display: none; }\nelement.classList.add("hidden");\nelement.classList.remove("hidden");</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Best Practice:</strong> Prefer CSS classes over inline styles for maintainability. \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const parent = document.querySelector(".container");\nconst newElement = document.createElement("div");\nnewElement.textContent = "New Element";\n\n// appendChild - add as last child\nparent.appendChild(newElement);\n\n// append - add multiple elements at end (newer)\nparent.append(newElement, "Some text", anotherElement);\n\n// prepend - add at beginning\nparent.prepend(newElement);\n\n// insertBefore - insert before specific element\nconst reference = document.querySelector(".reference");\nparent.insertBefore(newElement, reference);\n\n// Modern insertion methods\nconst box = document.querySelector(".box");\n\n// Insert relative to element\nbox.before(newElement);           // Before the element\nbox.after(newElement);            // After the element\nbox.prepend(newElement);          // Inside, at beginning\nbox.append(newElement);           // Inside, at end\n\n// replaceWith - replace element\nbox.replaceWith(newElement);\n\n// insertAdjacentHTML - insert HTML string\nconst container = child&lt;/p&gt;");\ncontainer.insertAdjacentHTML("beforeend", "&lt;p&gt;Last child&lt;/p&gt;");\ncontainer.insertAdjacentHTML("afterend", "&lt;p&gt;After container&lt;/p&gt;");\n\n// insertAdjacentElement - insert element\ncontainer.insertAdjacentElement("beforeend", newElement);</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Insertion Positions:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>beforebegin</code> - Before the element itself</li>\n                        <li><code>afterbegin</code> - Inside, before first child</li>\n                        <li><code>beforeend</code> - Inside, after last child</li>\n                    <pre><code>// Exercise: Build a dynamic product list\nconst products = [\n    { id: 1, name: "Laptop", price: 999, category: "Electronics" },\n    { id: 2, name: "Phone", price: 699, category: "Electronics" },\n    { id: 3, name: "Shirt", price: 29, category: "Clothing" },\n    { id: 4, name: "Book", price: 15, category: "Books" }\n];\n\n// Create product card\nfunction createProductCard(product) {\n    const card = document.createElement("div");\n    card.className = "product-card";\n    card.dataset.id = product.id;\n    \n    card.innerHTML = `\n        &lt;h3&gt;${product.name}&lt;/h3&gt;\n        &lt;p class="price"&gt;$${product.price}&lt;/p&gt;\n        &lt;p class="category"&gt;${product.category}&lt;/p&gt;\n        &lt;button class="add-to-cart"&gt;Add to Cart&lt;/button&gt;\n    `;\n    \n    return card;\n}\n\n// Render all products\nfunction renderProducts(products) {\n    const container = document.querySelector("#products");\n    container.innerHTML = "";\n    \n    products.forEach(product => {\n        const card = createProductCard(product);\n        container.appendChild(card);\n    });\n}\n\n// Filter by category\nfunction filterProducts(category) {\n    if (category === "all") return products;\n    return products.filter(p => p.category === category);\n}\n\n// Sort products\nfunction sortProducts(products, sortBy) {\n    const sorted = [...products];\n    switch(sortBy) {\n        case "price-asc":\n            return sorted.sort((a, b) => a.price - b.price);\n        case "price-desc":\n            return sorted.sort((a, b) => b.price - a.price);\n        case "name":\n            return sorted.sort((a, b) => a.name.localeCompare(b.name));\n        default:\n            return sorted;\n    }\n}\n\n// Initialize\nrenderProducts(products);\n\n// Event listeners for filters\ndocument.querySelector("#category-filter").addEventListener("change", (e) => {\n    const filtered = filterProducts(e.target.value);\n    const sortBy = document.querySelector("#sort-filter").value;\n    renderProducts(sortProducts(filtered, sortBy));\n});\n\ndocument.querySelector("#sort-filter").addEventListener("change", (e) => {\n    const category = document.querySelector("#category-filter").value;\n    const filtered = filterProducts(category);\n    renderProducts(sortProducts(filtered, e.target.value));\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <div When a user clicks a button, submits a form, presses a key, or loads a page - these are all events. Event handling is what makes web pages interactive and responsive to user actions.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Key Concept:</strong> JavaScript uses an event-driven model. Instead of constantly checking for changes, you register functions (event handlers) that are called when specific events occur.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Adding Event Listeners</h2>\n                <p>The modern way to handle events:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const button = document.querySelector("button");\n\n// addEventListener(event, function)\nbutton.addEventListener("click", function() {\n    console.log("Button clicked!");\n});\n\n// Arrow function syntax\nbutton.addEventListener("click", () => {\n    console.log("Button clicked!");\n});\n\n// Named function (can be reused and removed)\nfunction handleClick(event) {\n    console.log("Button clicked!", event);\n}\n\nbutton.addEventListener("click", handleClick);\n\n// Remove event listener\nbutton.removeEventListener("click", handleClick);\n\n// Multiple events on same element\nconst input = document.querySelector("input");\ninput.addEventListener("focus", () => console.log("Focused"));\ninput.addEventListener("blur", () => console.log("Blurred"));\ninput.addEventListener("input", () => console.log("Input changed"));</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>addEventListener Parameters:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>event</code> - Event type string (e.g., "click", "input")</li>\n                        <li><code>function</code> - Callback function to execute</li>\n                        <li><code>options</code> - Optional configuration object</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n\n                <h3>Event Options</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Run once and automatically remove\nbutton.addEventListener("click", () => {\n    console.log("This only runs once!");\n}, { once: true });\n\n// Capture phase (runs on parent first)\nparent.addEventListener("click", handler, { capture: true });\n\n// Passive event (won\'t call preventDefault)\ndocument.addEventListener("touchstart", handler, { passive: true });\n\n// Multiple options\nbutton.addEventListener("click", handler, {\n    once: true,\n    capture: true,\n    passive: true\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>The Event Object</h2>\n                <p>Every event handler receives an event object with useful information:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>button.addEventListener("click", (event) => {\n    // Event properties\n    console.log(event.type);          // "click"\n    console.log(event.target);        // Element that triggered event\n    console.log(event.currentTarget); // Element with listener\n    console.log(event.timeStamp);     // When event occurred\n    \n    // Mouse events\n    console.log(event.clientX, event.clientY);  // Position relative to viewport\n    console.log(event.pageX, event.pageY);      // Position relative to document\n    console.log(event.button);       // Which mouse button\n    \n    // Keyboard events\n    console.log(event.key);          // "Enter", "a", "ArrowUp"\n    console.log(event.code);         // "Enter", "KeyA", "ArrowUp"\n    console.log(event.ctrlKey);      // Was document.querySelector("form");\nform.addEventListener("submit", (event) => {\n    event.preventDefault();  // Stop form submission\n    console.log("Form submission prevented");\n});\n\n// Stop event from bubbling\ndocument.querySelector(".child").addEventListener("click", (event) => {\n    event.stopPropagation();  // Don\'t notify parent elements\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Common Event Properties:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>target</code> - The element that triggered the event</li>\n                        <li><code>currentTarget</code> - The element the listener is attached to</li>\n                        <li><code>preventDefault()</code> - Stop the default action</li>\n                        <li><code>stopPropagation()</code> - Stop event from bubbling</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Common Event Types</h2>\n                \n                <h3>Mouse Events</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const box = document.querySelector(".box");\n\nbox.addEventListener("click", (e) => {\n    console.log("Clicked!");\n});\n\nbox.addEventListener("dblclick", (e) => {\n    console.log("Double clicked!");\n});\n\nbox.addEventListener("mouseenter", (e) => {\n    console.log("Mouse entered");\n    box.classList.add("hovered");\n});\n\nbox.addEventListener("mouseleave", (e) => {\n    console.log("Mouse left");\n    box.classList.remove("hovered");\n});\n\nbox.addEventListener("mousemove", (e)          <h3>Keyboard Events</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const input = document.querySelector("input");\n\ninput.addEventListener("keydown", (e) =>          <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// DOM loaded\ndocument.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", () => {\n    console.log("DOM fully loaded");\n class="content-section">\n                <h2>Event Bubbling and Capturing</h2>\n                <p>Understand how events propagate through the DOM:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// HTML structure:\n// &lt;div id="grandparent"&gt;\n//     &lt;div id="parent"&gt;\n//         &lt;div id="child"&gt;Click me&lt;/div&gt;\n//     &lt;/div&gt;\n// &lt;/div&gt;\n\nconst grandparent = document.querySelector("#grandparent");\nconst parent = document.querySelector("#parent");\nconst child = document.querySelector("#child");\n\n// Bubbling phase (default) - child to parent\ngrandparent.addEventListener("click", () => console.log("Grandparent"));\nparent.addEventListener("click", () => console.log("Parent"));\nchild.addEventListener("click", () => console.log("Child"));\n\n// Clicking child outputs: Child → Parent → Grandparent\n\n// Capturing phase - parent to child\ngrandparent.addEventListener("click", () => console.log("Grandparent (capture)"), true);\nparent.addEventListener("click", () => console.log("Parent (capture)"), true);\nchild.addEventListener("click", () => console.log("Child (capture)"), true);\n\n// Clicking child outputs:\n// Grandparent (capture) → Parent (capture) → Child (capture)\n// Child → Parent → Grandparent (bubbling)\n\n// Stop propagation\nchild.addEventListener("click", (e) => {\n    e.stopPropagation();  // Event stops here\n    console.log("Child only");\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Event Propagation Phases:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Capturing:</strong> Event travels from window to target element</li>\n                        <li><strong>Target:</strong> Event reaches the target element</li>\n                        <li><strong>Bubbling:</strong> Event travels back up from target to window</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Event Delegation</h2>\n                <p>Handle events on parent instead of many children:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Instead of adding listeners to each button:\n// Bad approach (creates many listeners)\ndocument.querySelectorAll(".delete-btn").forEach(btn => {\n    btn.addEventListener("click", (e) => {\n        e.target.closest(".item").remove();\n    });\n});\n\n// Use event delegation (one listener on parent)\n// Good approach\ndocument.querySelector(".item-list").addEventListener("click", (e) => {\n    // Check if clicked element matches selector\n    if (e.target.matches(".delete-btn")) {\n        e.target.closest(".item").remove();\n    }\n});\n\n// Works for dynamically added elements too!\nfunction addItem(text) {\n    const item = document.createElement("li");\n    item.className = "item";\n    item.innerHTML = `\n        ${text}\n        &lt;button class="delete-btn"&gt;Delete&lt;/button&gt;\n    `;\n    document.querySelector(".item-list").appendChild(item);\n}\n\n// The delete button works immediately - no new listener needed!\n\n// Multiple handlers with delegation\ndocument.querySelector(".toolbar").addEventListener("click", (e) => {\n    const action = e.target.dataset.action;\n    \n    switch(action) {\n        case "bold":\n            document.execCommand("bold");\n            break;\n        case "italic":\n            document.execCommand("italic");\n            break;\n        case "underline":\n            document.execCommand("underline");\n            break;\n    }\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Benefits of Event Delegation:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Less memory (one listener instead of many)</li>\n                        <li>Works for dynamically added elements</li>\n                        <li>Less code to manage</li>\n                        <li>Easier to clean up</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Custom Events</h2>\n                <p>Create class="content-section">\n                <h2>Drag and Drop Events</h2>\n                <p>Create drag and drop interfaces:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const draggable = document.querySelector(".draggable");\nconst dropzone = document.querySelector(".dropzone");\n\n// Make element draggable\ndraggable.addEventListener("dragstart", (e) => {\n    e.dataTransfer.setData("text/plain", e.target.id);\n    e.target.classList.add("dragging");\n});\n\ndraggable.addEventListener("dragend", (e) => {\n    e.target.classList.remove("dragging");\n});\n\n// Dropzone events\ndropzone.addEventListener("dragover", (e) => {\n    e.preventDefault();  // Allow drop\n    dropzone.classList.add("drag-over");\n});\n\ndropzone.addEventListener("dragleave", (e) => {\n    dropzone.classList.remove("drag-over");\n});\n\ndropzone.addEventListener("drop", (e) => {\n    e.preventDefault();\n    dropzone.classList.remove("drag-over");\n    \n    const id = e.dataTransfer.getData("text/plain");\n    const element = document.getElementById(id);\n    dropzone.appendChild(element);\n});\n\n// Example: Sortable list\nconst list = document.querySelector(".sortable");\n\nlist.addEventListener("dragstart", (e) => {\n    if (e.target.matches("li")) {\n        e.dataTransfer.setData("text/plain", "");\n        e.target.classList.add("dragging");\n    }\n});\n\nlist.addEventListener("dragover", (e) => {\n    e.preventDefault();\n    const dragging = document.querySelector(".dragging");\n    const afterElement = getDragAfterElement(list, e.clientY);\n    \n    if (afterElement) {\n        list.insertBefore(dragging, afterElement);\n    } else {\n        list.appendChild(dragging);\n    }\n});\n\nfunction getDragAfterElement(container, y) {\n    const elements = [...container.querySelectorAll("li:not(.dragging)")];\n    \n    return elements.reduce((closest, child) => {\n        const box = child.getBoundingClientRect();\n        const offset = y - box.top - box.height / 2;\n        \n        if (offset < 0 && offset > closest.offset) {\n            return { offset, element: child };\n        }\n        return closest;\n    }, { offset: Number.NEGATIVE_INFINITY }).element;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Touch Events</h2>\n                <p>Handle touch interactions for mobile devices:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>const touchArea = document.querySelector(".touch-area");\n\ntouchArea.addEventListener("touchstart", (e) => {\n    const touch = e.touches[0];\n    console.log(`Touch started at: ${touch.clientX}, ${touch.clientY}`);\n});\n\ntouchArea.addEventListener("touchmove", (e) => {\n    e.preventDefault();  // Prevent scrolling while touching\n    const touch = e.touches[0];\n    console.log(`Touch moved to: ${touch.clientX}, ${touch.clientY}`);\n});\n\ntouchArea.addEventListener("touchend", (e) => {\n    console.log("Touch ended");\n});\n\n// Multi-touch\ntouchArea.addEventListener("touchstart", (e) => {\n    console.log(`Number of touches: ${e.touches.length}`);\n    \n    for (let touch of e.touches) {\n        console.log(`Touch ${touch.identifier}: ${touch.clientX}, ${touch.clientY}`);\n    }\n});\n\n// Swipe detection\nlet startX, startY;\n\ntouchArea.addEventListener("touchstart", (e) => {\n    startX = e.touches[0].clientX;\n    startY = e.touches[0].clientY;\n});\n\ntouchArea.addEventListener("touchend", (e) => {\n    if (!startX || !startY) return;\n    \n    const endX = e.changedTouches[0].clientX;\n    const endY = e.changedTouches[0].clientY;\n    \n    const diffX = endX - startX;\n    const diffY = endY - startY;\n    \n    if (Math.abs(diffX) > Math.abs(diffY)) {\n        // Horizontal swipe\n        if (diffX > 50) {\n            console.log("Swiped right");\n        } else if (diffX < -50) {\n            console.log("Swiped left");\n        }\n    } else {\n        // Vertical swipe\n        if (diffY > 50) {\n            console.log("Swiped down");\n        } else if (diffY < -50) {\n            console.log("Swiped up");\n        }\n    }\n    \n    startX = null;\n    startY = null;\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Performance: Debouncing and Throttling</h2>\n                <p>Optimize frequently firing events:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Debounce - wait until events stop firing\nfunction debounce(func, wait) {\n    let timeout;\n    return function executedFunction(...args) {\n        const later = () => {\n            clearTimeout(timeout);\n            func(...args);\n        };\n        clearTimeout(timeout);\n        timeout = setTimeout(later, wait);\n    };\n}\n\n// Throttle - limit how often function can run\nfunction throttle(func, limit) {\n    let inThrottle;\n    return function(...args) {\n        if (!inThrottle) {\n            func.apply(this, args);\n            inThrottle = true;\n            setTimeout(() => inThrottle = false, limit);\n        }\n    };\n}\n\n// Usage: Debounced search\nconst searchInput = document.querySelector("#search");\nsearchInput.addEventListener("input", debounce((e) => {\n    performSearch(e.target.value);\n}, 300));  // Wait 300ms after typing stops\n\n// Usage: Throttled scroll handler\nwindow.addEventListener("scroll", throttle(() => {\n    updateScrollIndicator();\n}, 100));  // Run at most every 100ms\n\n// Usage: Window resize\nwindow.addEventListener("resize", debounce(() => {\n    recalculateLayout();\n}, 250));</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>When to Use:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Debounce:</strong> Search input, resize, validation after typing</li>\n                        <li><strong>Throttle:</strong> Scroll events, mousemove, game loops</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Intersection Observer</h2>\n                <p>Efficiently detect element visibility:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Create observer\nconst observer = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {\n    entries.forEach(entry => {\n        if (entry.isIntersecting) {\n            console.log("Element is visible:", entry.target);\n            entry.target.classList.add("visible");\n            \n            // For one-time animations\n            // observer.unobserve(entry.target);\n        } else {\n            entry.target.classList.remove("visible");\n        }\n    });\n}, {\n    root: null,           // Viewport as root\n    rootMargin: "0px",    // Margin around root\n    threshold: 0.5        // Trigger when 50% visible\n});\n\n// Observe elements\ndocument.querySelectorAll(".animate-on-scroll").forEach(el => {\n    observer.observe(el);\n});\n\n// Lazy loading images\nconst imageObserver = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {\n    entries.forEach(entry => {\n        if (entry.isIntersecting) {\n            const img = entry.target;\n            img.src = img.dataset.src;  // Load image\n            img.classList.remove("lazy");\n            imageObserver.unobserve(img);\n        }\n    });\n});\n\ndocument.querySelectorAll("img.lazy").forEach(img => {\n    imageObserver.observe(img);\n});\n\n// Infinite scroll\nconst sentinel = document.querySelector("#sentinel");\nconst infiniteObserver = new IntersectionObserver((entries) => {\n    if (entries[0].isIntersecting) {\n        loadMoreContent();\n    }\n}, {\n    rootMargin: "100px"  // Load before reaching\n});\n\ninfiniteObserver.observe(sentinel);</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Practical }\n    });\n}\n\n// Example 2: Keyboard navigation\nfunction setupKeyboardNav() {\n    const items = document.querySelectorAll(".nav-item");\n    let currentIndex = 0;\n    \n      items[currentIndex].click();\n        }\n    });\n}\n\n// Example 3: Form validation\nfunction setupFormValidation() {\n    const form = document.querySelector("form");\n    \n    const \n    form.addEventListener("input", (e) => {\n        const input = e.target;\n        const rule = input.dataset.validate;\n        \n        if (validators[rule]) {\n            const isValid =     <pre><code>// Exercise: Build an interactive image gallery\nclass ImageGallery {\n    constructor(container) {\n        this.container = container;\n        this.images = &lt;img src="" alt="" class="modal-image"&gt;\n            &lt;button class="modal-next"&gt;›&lt;/button&gt;\n            &lt;div class="modal-counter"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\n        `;\n        \n However, many operations take time (like fetching data from a server). Asynchronous programming allows JavaScript to start a long-running task and continue executing other code while waiting for the result. This is essential for creating responsive applications.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Key Concept:</strong> Synchronous code runs line by line, blocking until complete. Asynchronous code starts an operation and continues, handling the result later when it\'s ready.\n                </div>\n\n                <h3>Synchronous vs Asynchronous</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Synchronous (blocking)\nconsole.log("Start");\nconsole.log("Middle");\nconsole.log("End");\n// Output: Start, Middle, End (in order, immediately)\n\n// Asynchronous (non-blocking)\nconsole.log("Start");\n\nsetTimeout(() => {\n    console.log("Middle");\n}, 1000);\n\nconsole.log("End");\n// Output: Start, End, Middle (Middle comes after 1 second)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Callbacks</h2>\n                <p>The traditional way to handle async operations:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Basic callback pattern\nfunction fetchData(callback) {\n    setTimeout(() => {\n        const data = { name: "John", age: 30 };\n        callback(data);\n    }, 1000);\n}\n\nfetchData((data) => {\n    console.log("Received:", data);\n});\n\n// Callback with error handling\nfunction fetchUser(id, onSuccess, onError) {\n    setTimeout(() => {\n        if (id > 0) {\n            onSuccess({ id, name: `User ${id}` });\n        } else {\n            onError("Invalid user ID");\n        }\n    }, 1000);\n}\n\nfetchUser(\n    1,\n    (user) => console.log("Success:", user),\n    (error) => console.log("Error:", error)\n);\n\n// Callback hell (pyramid of doom)\ngetUser(userId, (user) => {\n    getPosts(user.id, (posts) => {\n        getComments(posts[0].id, (comments) => {\n            getAuthor(comments[0].authorId, (author) => {\n                console.log(author.name);\n                // Deeper and deeper nesting...\n            });\n        });\n    });\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Callback Issues:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li>Deeply nested code becomes hard to read ("callback hell")</li>\n                        <li>Error handling must be done at every level</li>\n                        <li>Difficult to coordinate multiple async operations</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Promises</h2>\n                <p>A cleaner way to handle async operations:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Creating a Promise\nconst myPromise = new Promise((resolve, reject) => {\n    // Async operation\n    setTimeout(() => {\n        const success = true;\n        \n        if (success) {\n            resolve("Operation completed!");\n        } else {\n            reject("Operation failed!");\n        }\n    }, 1000);\n});\n\n// Using a Promise\nmyPromise\n    .then(result => {\n        console.log("Success:", result);\n        return result.toUpperCase();\n    })\n    .then(upperResult => {\n        console.log("Uppercase:", upperResult);\n    })\n    .catch(error => {\n        console.log("Error:", error);\n    })\n    .finally(() => {\n        console.log("Cleanup (runs always)");\n    });\n\n// Practical example: Fetch wrapper\nfunction fetchUser(id) {\n    return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {\n        setTimeout(() => {\n            if (id > 0) {\n                resolve({ id, name: `User ${id}` });\n            } else {\n                reject(new Error("Invalid user ID"));\n            }\n        }, 1000);\n    });\n}\n\nfetchUser(1)\n    .then(user => {\n        console.log("Found user:", user);\n        return fetchUser(2);  // Chain promises\n    })\n    .then(user2 => {\n        console.log("Found another user:", user2);\n    })\n    .catch(error => {\n        console.log("Error:", error.message);\n    });</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Promise States:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Pending:</strong> Initial state, operation in progress</li>\n                        <li><strong>Fulfilled:</strong> Operation completed successfully (resolved)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Rejected:</strong> Operation failed</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n\n                <h3>Promise Methods</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Promise.all - wait for all to complete\nconst p1 = Promise.resolve(1);\nconst p2 = Promise.resolve(2);\nconst p3 = new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(() => resolve(3), 1000));\n\nPromise.all([p1, p2, p3])\n    .then(results => {\n        console.log(results);  // [1, 2, 3]\n    });\n\n// If any rejects, all rejects\nPromise.all([\n    Promise.resolve(1),\n    Promise.reject("Error"),\n    Promise.resolve(3)\n])\n    .catch(error => console.log(error));  // "Error"\n\n// Promise.allSettled - wait for all, never rejects\nPromise.allSettled([\n    Promise.resolve(1),\n    Promise.reject("Error"),\n    Promise.resolve(3)\n])\n    .then(results => {\n        console.log(results);\n        // [\n        //   { status: "fulfilled", value: 1 },\n        //   { status: "rejected", reason: "Error" },\n        //   { status: "fulfilled", value: 3 }\n        // ]\n    });\n\n// Promise.race - first to settle wins\nPromise.race([\n    new Promise(r => setTimeout(() => r("slow"), 2000)),\n    new Promise(r => setTimeout(() => r("fast"), 1000))\n])\n    .then(result => console.log(result));  // "fast"\n\n// Promise.any - first to fulfill wins\nPromise.any([\n    Promise.reject("Error 1"),\n    Promise.resolve("Success"),\n    Promise.reject("Error 2")\n])\n    .then(result => console.log(result));  // "Success"\n\n// Promise.resolve and Promise.reject\nconst resolved = Promise.resolve("Instant value");\nconst rejected = Promise.reject("Instant error");</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Async/Await</h2>\n                <p>Write async code that looks synchronous:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Basic async/await\nasync function fetchUser(id) {\n    // Simulating API call\n    return new Promise(resolve => {\n        setTimeout(() => {\n            resolve({ id, name: `User ${id}` });\n        }, 1000);\n    });\n}\n\nasync function main() {\n    console.log("Fetching user...");\n    const user = await fetchUser(1);\n    console.log("Got user:", user);\n}\n\nmain();\n\n// Error handling with try/catch\nasync function fetchWithError() {\n    try {\n        const user = await fetchUser(-1);\n        console.log(user);\n    } catch (error) {\n        console.log("Caught error:", error.message);\n    } finally {\n        console.log("Cleanup");\n    }\n}\n\n// Parallel operations\nasync function fetchAllUsers() {\n    const [user1, user2, user3] = await Promise.all([\n        fetchUser(1),\n        fetchUser(2),\n        fetchUser(3)\n    ]);\n    \n    console.log(user1, user2, user3);\n}\n\n// Sequential vs Parallel\nasync function sequential() {\n    const start = Date.now();\n    \n    const a = await fetchUser(1);  // Wait 1 second\n    const b = await fetchUser(2);  // Wait another second\n    const c = await fetchUser(3);  // Wait another second\n    \n    console.log("Sequential:", Date.now() - start);  // ~3 seconds\n}\n\nasync function parallel() {\n    const start = Date.now();\n    \n    const [a, b, c] = await Promise.all([\n        fetchUser(1),\n        fetchUser(2),\n        fetchUser(3)\n    ]);\n    \n    console.log("Parallel:", Date.now() - start);  // ~1 second\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Async/Await Rules:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>async</code> keyword makes a function return a Promise</li>\n                        <li><code>await</code> pauses execution until Promise resolves</li>\n                        <li><code>await</code> can only be used inside <code>async</code> functions</li>\n                        <li>Use <code>try/catch</code> for error handling</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n\n                <h3>Advanced Patterns</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Loop with async/await\nasync function processItems(items) {\n    for (const item of items) {\n        await processItem(item);  // Process one at a time\n    }\n}\n\nasync function processItemsParallel(items) {\n    await Promise.all(items.map(item => processItem(item)));\n}\n\n// Sequential with reduce\nasync function processSequentially(items) {\n    await items.reduce(async (promise, item) => {\n        await promise;\n        return processItem(item);\n    }, Promise.resolve());\n}\n\n// Async generator\nasync function* fetchPages(url) {\n    let page = 1;\n    while (true) {\n        const data = await fetch(`${url}?page=${page}`);\n        if (data.items.length === 0) break;\n        yield data.items;\n        page++;\n    }\n}\n\n// Using async generator\nasync function getAllItems() {\n    const allItems = [];\n    for await (const items of fetchPages("/api/items")) {\n        allItems.push(...items);\n    }\n    return allItems;\n}\n\n// Top-level await (ES2022, in modules)\n// const data = await fetch(\'/api/data\');\n// console.log(data);\n\n// In non-module contexts, wrap in async IIFE\n(async () => {\n    const data = await fetch(\'/api/data\');\n    console.log(data);\n})();</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>The Event Loop</h2>\n                <p>Understand how JavaScript handles async operations:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Event loop demonstration\nconsole.log("1. Script start");\n\nsetTimeout(() => {\n    console.log("2. setTimeout");\n}, 0);\n\nPromise.resolve()\n    .then(() => console.log("3. Promise 1"))\n    .then(() => console.log("4. Promise 2"));\n\nconsole.log("5. Script end");\n\n// Output order:\n// 1. Script start\n// 5. Script end\n// 3. Promise 1\n// 4. Promise 2\n// 2. setTimeout\n\n// Why? Event loop priorities:\n// 1. Call stack (synchronous code)\n// 2. Microtask queue (Promises)\n// 3. Macrotask queue (setTimeout, setInterval)\n\n// Practical example\nasync function asyncFunction() {\n    console.log("async start");\n    await Promise.resolve();\n    console.log("async end");\n}\n\nnew Promise(resolve => {\n    console.log("promise constructor");\n    resolve();\n}).then(() => console.log("promise then"));\n\nconsole.log("main");\n\n// Output:\n// async start\n// promise constructor\n// main\n// async end\n// promise then</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Task Queues:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><strong>Call Stack:</strong> Where function execution happens</li>\n                        <li><strong>Microtask Queue:</strong> Promises, queueMicrotask (higher priority)</li>\n                        <li><strong>Macrotask Queue:</strong> setTimeout, setInterval, I/O operations</li>\n                        <li>Event loop processes: all sync code → all microtasks → one macrotask → repeat</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Error Handling Strategies</h2>\n                <p>Robust error handling for async code:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Pattern 1: try/catch\nasync function fetchSafe(url) {\n    try {\n        const response = await fetch(url);\n        if (!response.ok) {\n            throw new Error(`HTTP error: ${response.status}`);\n        }\n        return await response.json();\n    } catch (error) {\n        console.error("Fetch failed:", error);\n        throw error;  // Re-throw or return default\n    }\n}\n\n// Pattern 2: Higher-order function\nfunction withErrorHandling(asyncFn) {\n    return async (...args) => {\n        try {\n            return await asyncFn(...args);\n        } catch (error) {\n            console.error("Error in", asyncFn.name, error);\n            return null;  // Or some default value\n        }\n    };\n}\n\nconst safeFetch = withErrorHandling(fetch);\n\n// Pattern 3: Result object (like Rust)\nfunction Result(success, data, error) {\n    return { success, data, error };\n}\n\nasync function fetchWithResult(url) {\n    try {\n        const response = await fetch(url);\n        const data = await response.json();\n        return Result(true, data, null);\n    } catch (error) {\n        return Result(false, null, error.message);\n    }\n}\n\n// Usage\nconst result = await fetchWithResult("/api/data");\nif (result.success) {\n    console.log(result.data);\n} else {\n    console.log("Error:", result.error);\n}\n\n// Pattern 4: Retry logic\nasync function fetchWithRetry(url, maxRetries = 3) {\n    let lastError;\n    \n    for (let attempt = 1; attempt <= maxRetries; attempt++) {\n        try {\n            const response = await fetch(url);\n            if (!response.ok) {\n                throw new Error(`HTTP ${response.status}`);\n            }\n            return await response.json();\n        } catch (error) {\n            lastError = error;\n            console.log(`Attempt ${attempt} failed:`, error.message);\n            \n            if (attempt < maxRetries) {\n                await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, 1000 * attempt));\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    throw lastError;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Timing and Scheduling</h2>\n                <p>Control when code executes:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// setTimeout - run once after delay\nconst timeoutId = setTimeout(() => {\n    console.log("Delayed execution");\n}, 1000);\n\nclearTimeout(timeoutId);  // Cancel\n\n// setInterval - run repeatedly\nconst intervalId = setInterval(() => {\n    console.log("Repeating execution");\n}, 1000);\n\nclearInterval(intervalId);  // Stop\n\n// Request animation frame - synced with display refresh\nlet animationId;\nfunction animate() {\n    // Update animation\n    animationId = requestAnimationFrame(animate);\n}\nanimationId = requestAnimationFrame(animate);\ncancelAnimationFrame(animationId);\n\n// queueMicrotask - run before any macrotask\nqueueMicrotask(() => {\n    console.log("Runs before setTimeout");\n});\n\n// setImmediate (Node.js) - run after I/O\n// setImmediate(() => console.log("Immediate"));\n\n// Delay utility\nconst delay = ms => new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, ms));\n\nasync function example() {\n    console.log("Start");\n    await delay(1000);\n    console.log("After 1 second");\n}\n\n// Debounce async\nfunction debounceAsync(fn, delay) {\n    let timeoutId;\n    return async (...args) => {\n        clearTimeout(timeoutId);\n        return new Promise((resolve) => {\n            timeoutId = setTimeout(async () => {\n                resolve(await fn(...args));\n            }, delay);\n        });\n    };\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Concurrency Patterns</h2>\n                <p>Manage multiple async operations:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Limit concurrent operations\nasync function limitConcurrency(tasks, limit) {\n    const results = [];\n    const executing = [];\n    \n    for (const task of tasks) {\n        const promise = Promise.resolve().then(() => task());\n        results.push(promise);\n        \n        if (limit <= tasks.length) {\n            const exec = promise.then(() => {\n                executing.splice(executing.indexOf(exec), 1);\n            });\n            executing.push(exec);\n            \n            if (executing.length >= limit) {\n                await Promise.race(executing);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    return Promise.all(results);\n}\n\n// Simpler version with pool\nasync function asyncPool(poolLimit, array, iteratorFn) {\n    const ret = [];\n    const executing = new Set();\n    \n    for (const item of array) {\n        const p = Promise.resolve().then(() => iteratorFn(item));\n        ret.push(p);\n        executing.add(p);\n        \n        const cleanup = () => executing.delete(p);\n        p.then(cleanup).catch(cleanup);\n        \n        if (executing.size >= poolLimit) {\n            await Promise.race(executing);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    return Promise.all(ret);\n}\n\n// Usage: Fetch 100 URLs, max 5 at a time\nconst urls = Array.from({ length: 100 }, (_, i) => `/api/item/${i}`);\n\nawait asyncPool(5, urls, async (url) => {\n    const response = await fetch(url);\n    return response.json();\n});\n\n// Producer-consumer pattern\nclass AsyncQueue {\n    constructor() {\n        this.queue = [];\n        this.waiting = [];\n    }\n    \n    enqueue(item) {\n        if (this.waiting.length > 0) {\n            const resolve = this.waiting.shift();\n            resolve(item);\n        } else {\n            this.queue.push(item);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    dequeue() {\n        if (this.queue.length > 0) {\n            return Promise.resolve(this.queue.shift());\n        }\n        return new Promise(resolve => this.waiting.push(resolve));\n    }\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Practical Examples</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Example 1: Rate-limited API client\nclass RateLimitedClient {\n    constructor(baseUrl, requestsPerSecond = 5) {\n        this.baseUrl = baseUrl;\n        this.minInterval = 1000 / requestsPerSecond;\n        this.lastRequest = 0;\n    }\n    \n    async request(endpoint) {\n        const now = Date.now();\n        const waitTime = Math.max(0, this.minInterval - (now - this.lastRequest));\n        \n        if (waitTime > 0) {\n            await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, waitTime));\n        }\n        \n        this.lastRequest = Date.now();\n        const response = await fetch(this.baseUrl + endpoint);\n        return response.json();\n    }\n}\n\n// Example 2: Data fetching with cache\nclass DataFetcher {\n    constructor() {\n        this.cache = new Map();\n        this.pending = new Map();\n    }\n    \n    async fetch(url) {\n        // Check cache\n        if (this.cache.has(url)) {\n            return this.cache.get(url);\n        }\n        \n        // Check if request is already pending\n        if (this.pending.has(url)) {\n            return this.pending.get(url);\n        }\n        \n        // Make new request\n        const promise = fetch(url)\n            .then(r => r.json())\n            .then(data => {\n                this.cache.set(url, data);\n                this.pending.delete(url);\n                return data;\n            });\n        \n        this.pending.set(url, promise);\n        return promise;\n    }\n}\n\n// Example 3: Cancellable async operations\nclass CancellationToken {\n    constructor() {\n        this.cancelled = false;\n        this.listeners = [];\n    }\n    \n    cancel() {\n        this.cancelled = true;\n        this.listeners.forEach(fn => fn());\n    }\n    \n    throwIfCancelled() {\n        if (this.cancelled) {\n            throw new Error("Operation cancelled");\n        }\n    }\n    \n    async race(promise) {\n        return Promise.race([\n            promise,\n            new Promise((_, reject) => {\n                this.listeners.push(() => reject(new Error("Cancelled")));\n            })\n        ]);\n    }\n}\n\nasync function fetchWithCancellation(url, token) {\n    token.throwIfCancelled();\n    const response = await token.race(fetch(url));\n    token.throwIfCancelled();\n    return response.json();\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Practice Exercise</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Exercise: Build a data loading system\nclass DataLoader {\n    constructor() {\n        this.cache = new Map();\n        this.pending = new Map();\n        this.subscribers = new Map();\n    }\n    \n    // Fetch with caching\n    async load(key, fetcher) {\n        if (this.cache.has(key)) {\n            return this.cache.get(key);\n        }\n        \n        if (this.pending.has(key)) {\n            return this.pending.get(key);\n        }\n        \n        const promise = fetcher()\n            .then(data => {\n                this.cache.set(key, data);\n                this.pending.delete(key);\n                this.notifySubscribers(key, data);\n                return data;\n            })\n            .catch(error => {\n                this.pending.delete(key);\n                throw error;\n            });\n        \n        this.pending.set(key, promise);\n        return promise;\n    }\n    \n    // Subscribe to data changes\n    subscribe(key, callback) {\n        if (!this.subscribers.has(key)) {\n            this.subscribers.set(key, new Set());\n        }\n        this.subscribers.get(key).add(callback);\n        \n        // Return unsubscribe function\n        return () => {\n            this.subscribers.get(key).delete(callback);\n        };\n    }\n    \n    notifySubscribers(key, data) {\n        const callbacks = this.subscribers.get(key);\n        if (callbacks) {\n            callbacks.forEach(cb => cb(data));\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Invalidate cache\n    invalidate(key) {\n        this.cache.delete(key);\n    }\n    \n    // Prefetch data\n    async prefetch(keys, fetcher, concurrency = 3) {\n        const batches = [];\n        for (let i = 0; i < keys.length; i += concurrency) {\n            batches.push(keys.slice(i, i + concurrency));\n        }\n        \n        for (const batch of batches) {\n            await Promise.all(batch.map(key => this.load(key, () => fetcher(key))));\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// Test it\nconst loader = new DataLoader();\n\nloader.subscribe("users", (data) => {\n    console.log("Users updated:", data.length);\n});\n\nawait loader.load("users", () => \n    fetch("/api/users").then(r => r.json())\n);\n\nloader.invalidate("users");</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <div In web development, we commonly work with REST APIs that use HTTP methods to send and receive data. APIs let you fetch data from servers, submit forms, authenticate users, and interact with external services.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Key Concept:</strong> REST (Representational State Transfer) APIs use standard HTTP methods: GET (retrieve), POST (create), PUT (update), DELETE (remove). Data is typically exchanged in JSON format.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>The Fetch API</h2>\n                <p>The modern way to make HTTP requests in JavaScript:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Basic GET <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Common headers\nfetch("/api/data", {\n    headers: {\n        "Content-Type": "application/json",\n        "Accept": "application/json",\n        "Authorization": "Bearer your-token-here",\n        "X-API-Key": "your-api-key"\n    }\n});\n\n// Content types\n// JSON data\nheaders: { "Content-Type": "application/json" }\n\n// Form data\nheaders: { "Content-Type": "application/x-www-form-urlencoded" }\n\n// Multipart (file uploads)\nheaders: { "Content-Type": "multipart/form-data" }  // Browser sets automatically\n\n// Working     ...options.headers,\n            "Authorization": `Bearer ${token}`,\n            "Content-Type": "application/json"\n        }\n    });\n}\n\n// Handle different response types\nasync function (contentType?.includes("application/json")) {\n        return response.json();\n    } else if (contentType?.includes("text/")) {\n        return response.text();\n    } else if (contentType?.includes("blob")) {\n        return response.blob();\n    }\n    \n    return response.arrayBuffer();\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n    <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Single file upload\nasync function uploadFile(file) {\n    const formData = new FormData();\n    formData.append("file", file);\n xhr.addEventListener("error", () => reject(new Error("Upload failed")));\n        \n        const formData = new FormData();\n        formData.append("file", file);\n        \n        xhr.open("POST", e.target.files[0];\n    const result = await uploadWithProgress(file, (percent) => {\n        console.log(`Upload progress: ${percent.toFixed(1)}%`);\n    });\n    console.log("Upload complete:", result);\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Error Handling</h2>\n                <p>Robust error handling for API calls:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Comprehensive error handling\nclass APIError extends Error {\n    constructor(message, status, data) {\n        super(message);\n        this.name = "APIError";\n        this.status = status;\n        this.data = data;\n    }\n}\n\nasync function apiRequest(url, options = {}) {\n    try {\n        const response = await fetch(url, {\n            ...options,\n            headers: {\n                "Content-Type": "application/json",\n                ...options.headers\n            }\n        });\n        \n        // Parse response\n        const data = await response.json().catch(() => ({}));\n        \n        // Check for errors\n        if (!response.ok) {\n            throw new APIError(\n                data.message || "Request failed",\n                response.status,\n                data\n            );\n        }\n        \n        return data;\n        \n    } catch (error) {\n        if (error instanceof APIError) {\n            // API-specific errors\n            console.error(`API Error (${error.status}):`, error.message);\n        } else if (error.name === "TypeError") {\n            // Network errors\n            console.error("Network error:", error.message);\n        }\n        throw error;\n    }\n}\n\n// Handle specific status codes\nasync function handleErrors(response) {\n    switch (response.status) {\n        case 400:\n            throw new Error("Bad request - check your data");\n        case 401:\n            // Redirect to login\n            window.location.href = "/login";\n            throw new Error("Unauthorized - please log in");\n        case 403:\n            throw new Error("Forbidden - you don\'t have permission");\n        case 404:\n            throw new Error("Not found");\n        case 429:\n            throw new Error("Too many requests - please slow down");\n        case 500:\n            throw new Error("Server error - try again later");\n        default:\n            if (!response.ok) {\n                throw new Error(`HTTP error: ${response.status}`);\n            }\n    }\n    return response;\n}\n\n// Retry failed requests\nasync function fetchWithRetry(url, options = {}, retries = 3) {\n    for (let i = 0; i < retries; i++) {\n        try {\n            const response = await fetch(url, options);\n            if (response.ok) return response;\n        } catch (error) {\n            if (i === retries - 1) throw error;\n            await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, 1000 * (i + 1)));\n        }\n    }\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Building an API Client</h2>\n                <p>Create a reusable, organized API layer:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// API Client class\nclass APIClient {\n    constructor(baseUrl, defaultOptions = {}) {\n        this.baseUrl = baseUrl;\n        this.defaultOptions = defaultOptions;\n    }\n    \n    async request(endpoint, options = {}) {\n        const url = this.baseUrl + endpoint;\n        const config = {\n            ...this.defaultOptions,\n            ...options,\n            headers: {\n                ...this.defaultOptions.headers,\n                ...options.headers\n            }\n        };\n        \n        const response = await fetch(url, config);\n        \n        if value !== "") {\n            if (Array.isArray(value)) {\n                value.forEach(v => query.append(key, v));\n            } else {\n                query.set(key, value);\n            }\n        }\n    });\n    \n    return query.toString();\n}\n\n// Usage\nconst query = buildQuery({\n    page: 1,\n    tags: ["javascript", "react"],  // tags=javascript&tags=react\n    active: true,\n    empty: ""  // Skipped\n});</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>CORS and Proxy</h2>\n                <p>Handle cross-origin requests:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing)\n// Browsers block requests to different origins by default\n// Server must send appropriate headers:\n// Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *\n// Access-Control-Allow-Methods: GET, POST, PUT, DELETE\n// Access-Control-Allow-Headers: Content-Type, Authorization\n\n// Simple request (no preflight)\nfetch("https://api.example.com/data", {\n    method: "GET",\n    headers: {\n        "Accept": "application/json"\n    }\n});\n\n// Preflight request (browser sends OPTIONS first)\nfetch("https://api.example.com/data", {\n    method: "POST",\n    headers: {\n        "Content-Type": "application/json",\n        "Authorization": "Bearer token"\n    },\n    body: JSON.stringify({ data: "value" })\n});\n\n// Development proxy (vite.config.js)\n// export default {\n//     server: {\n//         proxy: {\n//             "/api": {\n//                 target: "https://api.example.com",\n//                 changeOrigin: true,\n//                 rewrite: (path) => path.replace(/^\\/api/, "")\n//             }\n//         }\n//     }\n// }\n\n// Runtime proxy function\nasync function proxyFetch(url, options = {}) {\n    const proxyUrl = "/api/proxy";\n    return fetch(proxyUrl, {\n        ...options,\n        headers: {\n            ...options.headers,\n            "X-Target-URL": url\n        }\n    });\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Simple in-memory cache\nconst cache = new Map();\n\nasync function fetchWithCache(url, options = {}) {\n    const cacheKey = JSON.stringify({ url, options });\n    \n    if (cache.has(cacheKey)) {\n        const { data, timestamp } = cache.get(cacheKey);\n        const age = Date.now() - timestamp;\n        \n        // Return if still fresh (5 minutes)\n        if (age < 5 * 60 * 1000) {\n            return data;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    const response = await fetch(url, options);\n    const data = await response.json();\n    \n    cache.set(cacheKey, {\n        data,\n        timestamp: Date.now()\n    });\n    \n    return data;\n}\n\n// Cache with TTL (Time To Live)\nclass CacheManager {\n    constructor(defaultTTL = 60000) {\n        this.cache = new Map();\n        this.defaultTTL = defaultTTL;\n    }\n    \n    set(key, value, ttl = this.defaultTTL) {\n        this.cache.set(key, {\n            value,\n            expiry: Date.now() + ttl\n        });\n    }\n    \n    get(key) {\n        const item = this.cache.get(key);\n        if (!item) return null;\n        \n        if (Date.now() > item.expiry) {\n            this.cache.delete(key);\n            return null;\n        }\n        \n        return item.value;\n    }\n    \n    delete(key) {\n        this.cache.delete(key);\n    }\n    \n    clear() {\n        this.cache.clear();\n    }\n}\n\n// Request deduplication\nconst pendingRequests = new Map();\n\nasync function deduplicatedFetch(url, options) {\n    if (pendingRequests.has(url)) {\n        return pendingRequests.get(url);\n    }\n    \n    const promise = fetch(url, options)\n        .then(r => r.json())\n        .finally(() => {\n            pendingRequests.delete(url);\n        });\n    \n    pendingRequests.set(url, promise);\n    return promise;\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n || 30;\n    \n    while (true) {\n        const data = await api.get(endpoint, {\n            ...params,\n            page,\n            per_page: perPage\n        });\n        \n        if     if (cacheKey) {\n            const cached = this.cache.get(cacheKey);\n            if (cached) return cached;\n        }\n        \n        const response = await fetch(url, {\n            ...options,\n            headers: {\n                "Content-Type": "application/json",\n                ...options.headers\n            }\n        });\n        \n        if (!response.ok) {\n            throw new Error(`HTTP ${response.status}: ${response.statusText}`);\n        }\n        \n        const data = await response.json();\n        \n        // Cache GET responses\n        if They can occur due to invalid user input, network failures, programming mistakes, or external service issues. Good error handling prevents crashes, provides helpful feedback to users, and makes debugging easier. In JavaScript, errors are objects that contain information about what went wrong.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <strong>Key Concept:</strong> Error handling is not just about preventing crashes—it\'s about creating a good user experience and making your code maintainable. Anticipate errors, handle them gracefully, and provide clear feedback.\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Error                <strong>Built-in Error Types:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>Error</code> - Generic error, base for all others</li>\n                        <li><code>SyntaxError</code> - Code parsing error (usually during development)</li>\n                        <li><code>ReferenceError</code> - Accessing undefined variable</li>\n                        <li><code>TypeError</code> - Operation on wrong type</li>\n                        <li><code>RangeError</code> - Value outside valid range</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>try...catch...finally</h2>\n                <p>The fundamental error handling structure:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Basic try...catch\ntry {\n    // Code that might throw an error\n    const result = JSON.parse(\'invalid json\');\n} catch (error) {\n    // Handle the error\n    console.log("Caught error:", error.message);\n}\n\n// try...catch...finally\ntry {\n    const data = riskyOperation();\n    processData(data);\n} catch (error) {\n    console.log("Error:", error.message);\n    notifyUser("Operation failed");\n} finally {\n    // Always runs, regardless of success or error\n    cleanup();\n}\n\n// Catch block only catches errors in the try block\ntry {\n    const result = divide(10, 0);\n    console.log(result);\n} catch (error) {\n    console.log("Division failed:", error.message);\n}\n\nfunction divide(a, b) {\n    if (b === 0) {\n        throw new Error("Cannot divide by zero");\n    }\n    return a / b;\n}\n\n// Nested try...catch\ntry {\n    try {\n        throw new Error("Inner error");\n    } catch (innerError) {\n        console.log("Inner catch:", innerError.message);\n        throw new Error("Re-thrown as outer error");\n    }\n} catch (outerError) {\n    console.log("Outer catch:", outerError.message);\n}</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <strong>Execution Flow:</strong>\n                    <ul>\n                        <li><code>try</code> - Code that might fail (required)</li>\n                        <li><code>catch</code> - Handles thrown errors (required if no finally)</li>\n                        <li><code>finally</code> - Cleanup code, always runs (optional)</li>\n                        <li>Only one of catch or finally is required</li>\n                    </ul>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Throwing Errors</h2>\n                <p>Create and throw your own errors:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Basic throw\nfunction validateAge(age) {\n    if (typeof age !== "number") {\n        throw new TypeError("Age must be a number");\n    }\n    if (age < 0 || age > 150) {\n        throw new RangeError("Age must be between 0 and 150");\n    }\n    return true;\n}\n\n// Throw custom error\nclass ApplicationError extends Error {\n    constructor(message, code, details = {}) {\n        super(message);\n        this.name = "ApplicationError";\n        this.code = code;\n        this.details = details;\n    }\n}\n\nfunction processPayment(amount, currency) {\n    if (amount <= 0) {\n        throw new ApplicationError(\n            "Invalid payment amount",\n            "INVALID_AMOUNT",\n            { amount, currency }\n        );\n    }\n    // Process payment\n}\n\n// Re-throwing errors\nasync function fetchUser(id) {\n    try {\n        const response = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);\n        const user = await response.json();\n        return user;\n    } catch (error) {\n        // Log the error\n        console.error("Failed to fetch user:", error);\n        // Re-throw with more context\n        throw new Error(`Failed to fetch user ${id}: ${error.message}`);\n    }\n}\n\n// Conditional throw\nfunction assert(condition, message) {\n    if (!condition) {\n        throw new Error(`Assertion failed: ${message}`);\n    }\n}\n\nassert(user.age >= 18, "User must be 18 or older");</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <section class="content-section">\n                <h2>Custom Error Classes</h2>\n                <p>Create specialized error types for your application:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Base application error\nclass AppError extends Error {\n    constructor(message, code, statusCode = 500) {\n        super(message);\n        this.name = this.constructor.name;\n        this.code = code;\n        this.statusCode = statusCode;\n        Error.captureStackTrace(this, this.constructor);\n    }\n}\n\n// Validation error\nclass ValidationError extends AppError {\n    constructor(message, field = null) {\n        super(message, "VALIDATION_ERROR", 400);\n        this.field = field;\n    }\n}\n\n// Not found error\nclass NotFoundError extends AppError {\n    constructor(resource, id) {\n        super(`${resource} with id \'${id}\' not found`, "NOT_FOUND", 404);\n        this.resource = resource;\n        this.resourceId = id;\n    }\n}\n\n// Authentication error\nclass AuthenticationError extends AppError {\n    constructor(message = "Authentication required") {\n        super(message, "AUTHENTICATION_ERROR", 401);\n    }\n}\n\n// Authorization error\nclass AuthorizationError extends AppError {\n    constructor(message = "Access denied") {\n        super(message, "AUTHORIZATION_ERROR", 403);\n    }\n}\n\n// Usage examples\nfunction findUser(id) {\n    const user = database.find(u => u.id === id);\n    if (!user) {\n        throw new NotFoundError("User", id);\n    }\n    return user;\n}\n\nfunction validateEmail(email) {\n    const emailRegex = /^[^\\s@]+@[^\\s@]+\\.[^\\s@]+$/;\n    if (!emailRegex.test(email)) {\n        throw new ValidationError("Invalid email format", "email");\n    }\n}\n\n// Error type checking\ntry {\n    findUser(999);\n} catch (error) {\n    if (error instanceof NotFoundError) {\n        console.log("Not found, show 404 page");\n    } else if (error instanceof ValidationError) {\n        console.log(`Invalid field: ${error.field}`);\n    } else {\n        console.log("Unknown error:", Catch, wrap, re-throw\nasync function getUserProfile(userId) {\n    try {\n        const user = await fetchUser(userId);\n        const posts = await fetchUserPosts(userId);\n        return { user, }\n    \n    if (!user.email || !isValidEmail(user.email)) {\n        throw new ValidationError("Valid email is required", "email");\n    }\n    \n    // Process user\n    return ${typeof value}`);\n    }\n}\n\nfunction assertInstance(value, constructor, name = "value") {\n    if (!(value instanceof constructor)) {\n        throw new TypeError(`${name} must be an instance of ${constructor.name}`);\n    }\n}\n\n// Usage\nfunction processData(data) {\n    assertType(data, "object", "data");\n    assertType(data.items, "object", "data.items");\n    assertInstance(data.items, Array, "data.items");\n    // Now safe to process\n}\n\n// Schema validation\nfunction validateUser(data) {\n    const schema = {\n        name: { type: "string", required: true, minLength: 2 },\n        email: { type: "string", required: true, pattern: /^[^\\s@]+@[^\\s@]+\\.[^\\s@]+$/ },\n        age: { type: "number", required: false, min: 0, max: 150 }\n    };\n    \n    const errors = [];\n    \n    for (const [field, rules] of Object.entries(schema)) {\n        const value = data[field];\n        \n        if (rules.required && (value === undefined || value === null || value === "")) {\n            errors.push({ field, message: `${field} is required` });\n            continue;\n        }\n        \n        if (value !== undefined) {\n            if (rules.type && typeof value !== rules.type) {\n                errors.push({ field, message: `${field} must be a ${rules.type}` });\n            }\n            \n            if (rules.minLength && value.length < rules.minLength) {\n                errors.push({ field, message: `${field} must be at least ${rules.minLength} characters` });\n            }\n            \n            if (rules.pattern && !rules.pattern.test(value)) errors.push({ field, message: `${field} must be at least ${rules.min}` });\n            }\n            \n            if (rules.max !== undefined && value > rules.max) {\n                errors.push({ field, message: `${field} must be at most ${rules.max}` });\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    return errors.length > 0 ? { valid: false, errors } : { valid: true };\n}\n\n// Usage\nconst class="content-section">\n                <h2>Error Recovery Strategies</h2>\n                <p>Handle errors gracefully and recover:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>// Retry with backoff\nasync function retryWithBackoff(fn, maxRetries = 3, baseDelay = 1000) {\n    let lastError;\n    \n    for (let attempt = 0; attempt < maxRetries; attempt++) {\n        try {\n            return await fn();\n        } catch (error) {\n            lastError = error;\n            \n            if (attempt < maxRetries - 1) {\n                const delay = baseDelay * Math.pow(2, attempt);\n                console.log(`Attempt ${attempt + 1} failed, retrying in ${delay}ms`);\n                await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, delay));\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    throw lastError;\n}\n\n// Fallback values\nfunction getConfigValue(key) {\n    try {\n        const config = JSON.parse(localStorage.getItem("config"));\n        return config[key];\n    } catch {\n        return DEFAULT_CONFIG[key];  // Fallback\n    }\n}\n\n// Circuit breaker pattern\nclass CircuitBreaker {\n    constructor(fn, options = {}) {\n        this.fn = fn;\n        this.failureThreshold = options.failureThreshold || 5;\n        this.resetTimeout = options.resetTimeout || 60000;\n        this.failures = 0;\n        this.state = "closed";  // closed, open, half-open\n        this.lastFailure = null;\n    }\n    \n    async execute(...args) {\n        if (this.state === "open") {\n            if (Date.now() - this.lastFailure > this.resetTimeout) {\n                this.state = "half-open";\n            } else {\n                throw new Error("Circuit breaker is open");\n            }\n        }\n        \n        try {\n            const result = await this.fn(...args);\n            this.onSuccess();\n            return result;\n        } catch (error) {\n            this.onFailure();\n            throw error;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    onSuccess() {\n        this.failures = 0;\n        this.state = "closed";\n    }\n    \n    onFailure() {\n        this.failures++;\n        this.lastFailure = Date.now();\n        \n        if (this.failures >= this.failureThreshold) {\n            this.state = "open";\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// Graceful degradation\nclass FeatureFlags {\n    constructor() {\n        this.flags = {};\n    }\n    \n    async checkFeature(name, fallback = false) {\n        try {\n            const response = await fetch(`/api/features/${name}`);\n            const data = await response.json();\n            return data.enabled;\n        } catch {\n            return fallback;  // Fallback if API fails\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nasync function renderPage() {\n    const showNewFeature = await featureFlags.checkFeature("new-ui", false);\n    \n    if (showNewFeature) {\n        renderNewUI();\n    } else {\n        renderOldUI();\n    }\n}</code></pre>\n
